<div id="review_2352795918" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352795918" />
    <a title="Shayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15058212-shayla"><img alt="Shayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513191429p2/15058212.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352795918?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shayla" href="/user/show/15058212-shayla">Shayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15058212-shayla?shelf=favorite-fantasy">favorite-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15058212-shayla?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352795918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15568750772298399081">(spoilers ahead)<br/><br/>THAT WAS AMAZING!!!! Just absolutely epic and thrilling, I LOVED it. Every book just gets better and better. I don't think I was so sure about Karigan as a heroine (thought she was a little boring in book 1) but I'm 100% on board with it now. She's exactly the kind of character I want when I'm reading high fantasy like this: living legend. She's so bold and courageous, someone who will be spoken about for generations, who has songs composed about her insane journeys and extraordi</span>
  <span id="freeText15568750772298399081" style="display:none">(spoilers ahead)<br /><br />THAT WAS AMAZING!!!! Just absolutely epic and thrilling, I LOVED it. Every book just gets better and better. I don't think I was so sure about Karigan as a heroine (thought she was a little boring in book 1) but I'm 100% on board with it now. She's exactly the kind of character I want when I'm reading high fantasy like this: living legend. She's so bold and courageous, someone who will be spoken about for generations, who has songs composed about her insane journeys and extraordinary deeds. I mean I'm sure some people out there would complain about Karigan being overpowered or a Mary-Sue or whatEVER but I just do not care. You think I'm reading high fantasy for realism? No, binch! I'm reading it for escapism! Drag me out of my boring ass life and into a story! Make me sit down and read for 6 hours straight! <br /><br />Anyway, so good, 10/10 would read again. My only complaint is that most of the time im just not on board with our main romance, which as far as I can tell is VERY popular with other readers. King Zach just doesn't do it for me! I'm TIRED of the whole commoner-royal thing, Karigan should fall in love with a Weapon or another green rider or not fall in love at all. I do like Zachary/Karigan when we get his pov on it, but that is not often at all. I would greatly prefer Amberhill over him. Other than that, PERFECT, wouldn't change a thing. Made me stay up til 2 am when I have an 8 am shift to get to. Thanks Ms. Britain! <br /><br />Sidenotes:<br />•I will ALWAYS love any sort of training scenes in high fantasy. Seeing characters learn to fight is always a highlight of any story for me. <br /><br />•bring Alton and Karigan together again next book please???<br /><br />•I love that so far every book has a scene at the end that is just absolutely WILD and out of the left field. Like okay first she rides with the spirits of long dead riders and now Karigan is interacting with gods? Cool, love it. Hope this trend continues<br /><br />•Generally I'm not a fan of supernatural stuff but that's a big part of why I like this story<br /><br />•Trying really hard to like Estora but I just can't like rich people sorry <br /><br />•I'm obsessed with knights so the fact that Karigan got knighted???????? Killed me. I was definitely crying. This book really reminded me of the Damar books. <br /><br />•my whole reaction to this series is just GOD, I wish that were me. I mean I could never do what Karigan does, but I wish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15568750772298399081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143788821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143788821" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4877728-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579291918p2/4877728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143788821?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/4877728-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101215586" href="/book/show/9284078-the-high-king-s-tomb">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877728-melissa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143788821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2710461377004843113">An amazing story, but still not as good as the first in the series. While it had all the wonderful characters of the first two (and the addition of a few more) the plot line was hard to follow and somewhat confusing.<br/><br/>As a recap (and possible spoiler) of the first two books, Karigan has been kicked out of school and on her way back to her father's city she encounters a Green Rider who is mortally injured. The Green Rider's are the King's personal messengers and as part of this service, they obtain</span>
  <span id="freeText2710461377004843113" style="display:none">An amazing story, but still not as good as the first in the series. While it had all the wonderful characters of the first two (and the addition of a few more) the plot line was hard to follow and somewhat confusing.<br /><br />As a recap (and possible spoiler) of the first two books, Karigan has been kicked out of school and on her way back to her father's city she encounters a Green Rider who is mortally injured. The Green Rider's are the King's personal messengers and as part of this service, they obtain small magical powers. Karigan agrees to take up his message and deliver it to the King at all costs. She succeeds, despite many trials, and then later has to help him fight for his throne as his evil brother tries to take it from him.<br /><br />The next book has Karigan returning to the Green Rider's to join permanently as she can no longer resist the call. On an expedition, her party releases a wraith who intends to do harm from the realm along with Mornhavon the Black, an evil sorcerer who dwells behind a magical wall. The wall is starting to fall apart and the rider's magic is starting to fail them. Despite this, with the help of a ghost, Karigan is able to send Mornhavon into the future so they can develop a plan in the present to defeat him.<br /><br />Which leads us to this book. New riders are joining the ranks everyday and Karigan finds herself accompanying one of them to train him on a three part errand run. She is in search of an important book that will help heal the wall, has to obtain new horses for the riders, and must go in search of a missing rider. If that weren't enough, she encounters plenty of danger and intrigue along the way as well. Most prominently featured is Salvistar, the horse of the death god, who has taken an interest in her despite her wanting nothing to do with him.<br /><br />This book also covers the story of Alton, one of the D'Yer's whose job is to fix the wall and keep it maintained. Blocked from the wall by a vengeful cousin, he can only rely on third hand knowledge to try and save it. In addition to this he must overcome his feelings of Karigan and the "betrayal" she enacted upon him.<br /><br />There are some other side plots as well, but honestly, I could have done without them. I feel they took away from the plot and while its nice to see the view of the enemy, it just didn't seem necessary for this story. The same goes for the subplot of the King's betrothed as well. While it was an integral part of the story it would have been fine just to mention it rather than show her point of view. Because of all these different point of views, the book was hard to follow and I found myself getting lost as the chapters would go three in a row of one person, one of another, two of another, and etc. There was no reason to it or even a pattern to rely on.<br /><br />The characters were better described in this book as compared to the second. I was able to get a better description of Karigan and have a vague idea of what she looks like now. In addition, Alton is described remarkably well and it is easy to see his progression from shabby to not so shabby. The rest of the book had plenty of description as well. As far as squeamishness and vivid writing, this book did not contain as much violence or battles and so was easier to read in that aspect. There was not much bloodiness at all.<br /><br />I grew to love Karigan even more in this novel. She seems like a real person and not just a perfect heroine. She has doubts and second thoughts but still manages to pull it all together and do the right thing. This book also introduced two characters I absolutely loved. Damien and his Lady, the horse sellers of the Rider's steeds. These two are so darn cute that I couldn't help but smile when they were talking to each other. Britain does a good job of letting the reader see just how much Damien loves his woman. This book also brought back the characters of Miss Bay and Miss Bunch. They were barely mentioned which was somewhat disappointing, but at leas they were there.<br /><br />Overall I was pleased with how this novel turned out. It describes a great bit of plot and continues the story well. It does leave a lot unfinished however, and before reading I hadn't realized that there would be more than three books in this series. It appears the next one will be out early 2011 and I can't wait to see how the story continues!<br /><br />The High King's Tomb<br />Copyright 2007<br />679 pages </span>
  <a data-text-id="2710461377004843113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cXqsD9T6oOM+BBebJbMztDTr6dhJ0aWqg5NQVStLItyAS/3Q1tONpRWgnEQ2j0+buRxcPaatGeQus9IijKhx/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l9svoGH+5O/1BkvhkIcXTGq1Dx6/JcW2FzDpjrMywg1m6n5/Y9fJqd6iwD6Du2tj50K6+1BZefi6EGv5FNGRLg==')})
  }

For he had come to learn that a powerful and unethical magical order, the Magi, were controlling Alta by systematically draining the other, gentler, magical orders of their powers--thus strengthening themselves.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/85545.Kristen_Britain">About Kristen Britain</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/85545.Kristen_Britain"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1266020934p3/85545.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/85545.Kristen_Britain">Kristen Britain

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7253691708065089783">Kristen Britain grew up in the Finger Lakes region of New York State, where she started her first novel - an undersea fantasy featuring herself and her friends - at the age of nine. She published her first book, a cartoon collection called Horses and Horsepeople, at the age of thirteen. After completing her degree in film production at Ithaca College in 1987 she made the logical (?!) leap from cin</span>
  <span id="freeText7253691708065089783" style="display:none">Kristen Britain grew up in the Finger Lakes region of New York State, where she started her first novel - an undersea fantasy featuring herself and her friends - at the age of nine. She published her first book, a cartoon collection called Horses and Horsepeople, at the age of thirteen. After completing her degree in film production at Ithaca College in 1987 she made the logical (?!) leap from cinema to the National Park Service. Her many years as a park ranger enabled her to work in a variety of natural and historical settings, from 300 feet below the surface of the Earth to 13,000 feet above sea level on the Continental Divide; and from the textile mills of the American Industrial Revolution to the homes of Americans who changed the course of history. <br /><br />Currently she lives in a log cabin in Maine where she writes full time and pursues interests reading, guitar playing, and cartoon illustration, supervised by a cat and a dog. She enjoys exploring the magical places around her and can often be found paddling a canoe in stillwater, ambling through the woods to mountain summits, or sitting along the rocky shore listening, watching, and daydreaming. This is her fantasy, at least. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7253691708065089783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
